"<p>1. dynasty /ˈdaɪnəsti/ (n): triều đại</p>
<p>The Mogul dynasty ruled over India for centuries.</p>
<p>2. dynastic (adj) /daɪˈnæstɪk/: thuộc về triều đại</p>
<p>His dynastic ties to business gave him his career in oil.</p>
<p>One of the functions of women in dynastic positions was to marry and produce children who would become the heirs.</p>
<p>Dynastic politics is hardly a new development in America.</p>
<p>3. cultural /ˈkʌltʃərəl/ (adj): thuộc về văn hóa</p>
<p>It is a study of the social and cultural milieu in which Michelangelo lived and worked.</p>
<p>The country is now a cultural and social mosaic due to the influx of several different ethnic groups.</p>
<p>4. culturally (adv) /ˈkʌltʃərəli/: về mặt văn hóa</p>
<p>The bay was culturally significant for the Aboriginal people.</p>
<p>Culturally speaking, women here are treated unequally.</p>
<p>What we expect of families is so culturally specific.</p>
<p>5. culture (n/v) /ˈkʌltʃər/: văn hóa - (v): cày cấy, trồng trọt</p>
<p>American culture has been exported all over the world.</p>
<p>She got some books out of the library and immersed herself in Jewish history and culture.</p>
<p>It's a nostalgia trip back into the youth culture of the swinging 60s.</p>
<p>Surely it is wrong to try to impose western culture on these people?</p>
<p>Each culture had a special ritual to initiate boys into manhood.</p>
<p>6. cultured (adj) /ˈkʌltʃərd /: có giáo dục, có văn hoá</p>
<p>A cultured person has had a good education and knows a lot about art, music, literature, etc.</p>
<p>7. representative /ˌreprɪˈzentətɪv/ (n): miêu tả; thể hiện,  đại diện cho một giai cấp hoặc một nhóm - (n):  người đại biểu, người đại diện</p>
<p>A representative from the tour company will meet you at the check-in.</p>
<p>He visited China in his official capacity as America's trade representative.</p>
<p>We have representatives operating in most countries.</p>
<p>8. represent (v) /ˌreprɪˈzent /: miêu tả, hình dung,  đại diện cho, là hình tượng của, tượng trưng cho; biểu trưng</p>
<p>They chose a famous barrister to represent them in court.</p>
<p>Union officials representing the teachers met the government today.</p>
<p>I sent my husband to represent me at the funeral.</p>
<p>9. representation (n) /ˌreprɪzenˈteɪʃn/: sự thay mặt, sự đại diện; sự làm phát ngôn viên cho; những người đại diện</p>
<p>Defendants have a right to legal representation and must be informed of that right when they are arrested.</p>
<p>The farmers demanded greater representation in parliament.</p>
<p>The main opposing parties have nearly equal representation in the legislature.</p>
<p>The scheme is intended to increase representation of minority groups.</p>
<p>The members are chosen by a system of proportional representation.</p>
<p>10. representational (adj) /ˌreprɪzenˈteɪʃənl/: tiêu biểu, tượng trưng, đại diện, thay mặt</p>
<p>The few differences that were found between the two data sets are unlikely to have a representational origin.</p>
<p>11. behaviour /bɪˈheɪvjər/ (n): lối hành xử</p>
<p>Her behaviour is often appalling.</p>
<p>He was notorious for his violent and threatening behaviour.</p>
<p>12. behave (v) /bɪˈheɪv/: cư xử</p>
<p>She always behaves well/badly when her aunts come to visit.</p>
<p>Whenever there was a full moon he would start behaving strangely.</p>
<p>They behaved as if nothing had happened.</p>
<p>13. behavioural (adj) /bɪˈheɪvjərəl/: hành vi</p>
<p>She studied behavioral psychology in college.</p>
<p>14. behaviourally (adv) /bɪˈheɪvjərəli/: về mặt hành vi</p>
<p>The participant experts stressed the importance of confidentiality and behaviorally-based feedback.</p>
<p>15. behaviourism (n) /bɪˈheɪvjərɪzəm/: chủ nghĩa hành vi</p>
<p>Most psychology research at the time was focused on behaviorism -- classical conditioning and the like.</p>
<p>16. behaviourist (n) /bɪˈheɪvjərɪst /: nhà hành vi học</p>
<p>Primate tool use has been studied by animal behaviorists.</p>
<p>As a practicing canine behaviorist, I have seen a steady increase in behavior problems.</p>
<p>Seek advice from a vet, animal behaviorist, or reputable dog trainer.</p>
<p>17. memorialize /məˈmɔːriəlaɪz/ (v): tôn vinh, tưởng nhớ</p>
<p>A local artist was commissioned by the community to memorialize the war dead.</p>
<p>18. memorably (adv) /ˈmemərəbli/: đáng nhớ</p>
<p>It was no dishonor to finish out of the medals in the most memorable 100 metres race ever seen.</p>
<p>The lavish production makes this musical truly memorable.</p>
<p>On this memorable occasion we salute the wonderful work done by the association.</p>
<p>19. memorial (n) /məˈmɔːriəl/: đài kỷ niệm</p>
<p>The war memorial was erected in 1950.</p>
<p>The war memorial was dedicated to both Jews and Gentiles.</p>
<p>The chapel was raised as a memorial to her son.</p>
<p>10. memory (n) /ˈmeməri/: kỷ niệm, ký ức</p>
<p>I have a good memory and am able to retain facts easily.</p>
<p>Loss of memory is a natural part of old age.</p>
<p>That last conversation we had is engraved on my memory forever.</p>
<p>21. brilliant /ˈbrɪliənt / (adj): lỗi lạc</p>
<p>Her mother was a brilliant scientist.</p>
<p>He gave a brilliant performance.</p>
<p>The idea was quite brilliant.</p>
<p>22. brilliance (n) /ˈbrɪliəns/: sáng chói</p>
<p>Her first novel showed signs of brilliance.</p>
<p>23. brilliantly (adv) /ˈbrɪliəntli/: rựa rỡ</p>
<p>He seems to do everything brilliantly - piano playing, skiing, sailing.</p>
<p>The novel brilliantly captures the complex feel of modern life.</p>
<p>The ploy worked brilliantly.</p>
<p>24. scholar /ˈskɑːlər/ (n): học giả</p>
<p>Most scholars assert that Christ was born somewhere around this time.</p>
<p>The theory has been widely discredited by scholars.</p>
<p>25. scholarly (adj) /ˈskɑːlərli/: biểu lộ học vấn, sự thận trọng và chu đáo điển hình của một học giả; có tính học thuật; khoa học; uyên thâm</p>
<p>John is more serious and scholarly than his brother.</p>
<p>Her research was published in a scholarly journal.</p>
<p>26. scholarship (n) /ˈskɑːlərʃɪp/: học bổng</p>
<p>He got /won a scholarship to Harvard.</p>
<p>Paula went to the Royal College of Music on a scholarship.</p>
<p>27. achievement /əˈtʃiːvmənt / (n): thành tích</p>
<p>An Olympic silver medal is a remarkable achievement for one so young.</p>
<p>The Tale of Genji has been described as the greatest achievement of Japanese literature.</p>
<p>It gives you a sense of achievement if you actually make it to the end of a very long book.</p>
<p>28. achieve (v) /əˈtʃiːv/: đạt được</p>
<p>The government's training policy, he claimed, was achieving its objectives.</p>
<p>She finally achieved her ambition to visit South America.</p>
<p>I've been working all day, but I feel as if I've achieved nothing.</p>
<p>29. achiever (n) /əˈtʃiːvər/: người đạt được thành tựu</p>
<p>All the women interviewed were achievers in their chosen field.</p>
<p>High achievers traditionally come from middle-class areas and go to university rather than colleges.</p>
<p>30. achievable (adj) /əˈtʃiːvəbl/: có thể đạt được</p>
<p>Before you set your targets, make sure that they are achievable.</p>
<p>31. engrave /ɪnˈɡreɪv/ (v): khắc, trạm trổ</p>
<p>The jeweller skilfully engraved the initials on the ring.</p>
<p>The bracelet was engraved with his name and date of birth.</p>
<p>32. engraver /ɪnˈɡreɪvər/ (n): thợ khắc</p>
<p>Only three engravers in the pottery industry are involved in the whole of the year.</p>
<p>33. engraving (n) /ɪnˈɡreɪvɪŋ/: tranh điêu khắc</p>
<p>The museum owns many fine 18th-century engravings.</p>
<p>The book describes the art of engraving.</p>"

<p>2. dynastic (adj) /daɪˈnæstɪk/: thuộc về triều đại</p>
<p>His dynastic ties to business gave him his career in oil.</p>
<p>One of the functions of women in dynastic positions was to marry and produce children who would become the heirs.</p>
<p>Dynastic politics is hardly a new development in America.</p>
<p>3. cultural /ˈkʌltʃərəl/ (adj): thuộc về văn hóa</p>
<p>It is a study of the social and cultural milieu in which Michelangelo lived and worked.</p>
<p>The country is now a cultural and social mosaic due to the influx of several different ethnic groups.</p>
<p>4. culturally (adv) /ˈkʌltʃərəli/: về mặt văn hóa</p>
<p>The bay was culturally significant for the Aboriginal people.</p>
<p>Culturally speaking, women here are treated unequally.</p>
<p>What we expect of families is so culturally specific.</p>
<p>5. culture (n/v) /ˈkʌltʃər/: văn hóa - (v): cày cấy, trồng trọt</p>
<p>American culture has been exported all over the world.</p>
<p>She got some books out of the library and immersed herself in Jewish history and culture.</p>
<p>It's a nostalgia trip back into the youth culture of the swinging 60s.</p>
<p>Surely it is wrong to try to impose western culture on these people?</p>
<p>Each culture had a special ritual to initiate boys into manhood.</p>
<p>6. cultured (adj) /ˈkʌltʃərd /: có giáo dục, có văn hoá</p>
<p>A cultured person has had a good education and knows a lot about art, music, literature, etc.</p>
<p>7. representative /ˌreprɪˈzentətɪv/ (n): miêu tả; thể hiện,  đại diện cho một giai cấp hoặc một nhóm - (n):  người đại biểu, người đại diện</p>
<p>A representative from the tour company will meet you at the check-in.</p>
<p>He visited China in his official capacity as America's trade representative.</p>
<p>We have representatives operating in most countries.</p>
<p>8. represent (v) /ˌreprɪˈzent /: miêu tả, hình dung,  đại diện cho, là hình tượng của, tượng trưng cho; biểu trưng</p>
<p>They chose a famous barrister to represent them in court.</p>
<p>Union officials representing the teachers met the government today.</p>
<p>I sent my husband to represent me at the funeral.</p>
<p>9. representation (n) /ˌreprɪzenˈteɪʃn/: sự thay mặt, sự đại diện; sự làm phát ngôn viên cho; những người đại diện</p>
<p>Defendants have a right to legal representation and must be informed of that right when they are arrested.</p>
<p>The farmers demanded greater representation in parliament.</p>
<p>The main opposing parties have nearly equal representation in the legislature.</p>
<p>The scheme is intended to increase representation of minority groups.</p>
<p>The members are chosen by a system of proportional representation.</p>
<p>10. representational (adj) /ˌreprɪzenˈteɪʃənl/: tiêu biểu, tượng trưng, đại diện, thay mặt</p>
<p>The few differences that were found between the two data sets are unlikely to have a representational origin.</p>
<p>11. behaviour /bɪˈheɪvjər/ (n): lối hành xử</p>
<p>Her behaviour is often appalling.</p>
<p>He was notorious for his violent and threatening behaviour.</p>
<p>12. behave (v) /bɪˈheɪv/: cư xử</p>
<p>She always behaves well/badly when her aunts come to visit.</p>
<p>Whenever there was a full moon he would start behaving strangely.</p>
<p>They behaved as if nothing had happened.</p>
<p>13. behavioural (adj) /bɪˈheɪvjərəl/: hành vi</p>
<p>She studied behavioral psychology in college.</p>
<p>14. behaviourally (adv) /bɪˈheɪvjərəli/: về mặt hành vi</p>
<p>The participant experts stressed the importance of confidentiality and behaviorally-based feedback.</p>
<p>15. behaviourism (n) /bɪˈheɪvjərɪzəm/: chủ nghĩa hành vi</p>
<p>Most psychology research at the time was focused on behaviorism -- classical conditioning and the like.</p>
<p>16. behaviourist (n) /bɪˈheɪvjərɪst /: nhà hành vi học</p>
<p>Primate tool use has been studied by animal behaviorists.</p>
<p>As a practicing canine behaviorist, I have seen a steady increase in behavior problems.</p>
<p>Seek advice from a vet, animal behaviorist, or reputable dog trainer.</p>
<p>17. memorialize /məˈmɔːriəlaɪz/ (v): tôn vinh, tưởng nhớ</p>
<p>A local artist was commissioned by the community to memorialize the war dead.</p>
<p>18. memorably (adv) /ˈmemərəbli/: đáng nhớ</p>
<p>It was no dishonor to finish out of the medals in the most memorable 100 metres race ever seen.</p>
<p>The lavish production makes this musical truly memorable.</p>
<p>On this memorable occasion we salute the wonderful work done by the association.</p>
<p>19. memorial (n) /məˈmɔːriəl/: đài kỷ niệm</p>
<p>The war memorial was erected in 1950.</p>
<p>The war memorial was dedicated to both Jews and Gentiles.</p>
<p>The chapel was raised as a memorial to her son.</p>
<p>10. memory (n) /ˈmeməri/: kỷ niệm, ký ức</p>
<p>I have a good memory and am able to retain facts easily.</p>
<p>Loss of memory is a natural part of old age.</p>
<p>That last conversation we had is engraved on my memory forever.</p>
<p>21. brilliant /ˈbrɪliənt / (adj): lỗi lạc</p>
<p>Her mother was a brilliant scientist.</p>
<p>He gave a brilliant performance.</p>
<p>The idea was quite brilliant.</p>
<p>22. brilliance (n) /ˈbrɪliəns/: sáng chói</p>
<p>Her first novel showed signs of brilliance.</p>
<p>23. brilliantly (adv) /ˈbrɪliəntli/: rựa rỡ</p>
<p>He seems to do everything brilliantly - piano playing, skiing, sailing.</p>
<p>The novel brilliantly captures the complex feel of modern life.</p>
<p>The ploy worked brilliantly.</p>
<p>24. scholar /ˈskɑːlər/ (n): học giả</p>
<p>Most scholars assert that Christ was born somewhere around this time.</p>
<p>The theory has been widely discredited by scholars.</p>
<p>25. scholarly (adj) /ˈskɑːlərli/: biểu lộ học vấn, sự thận trọng và chu đáo điển hình của một học giả; có tính học thuật; khoa học; uyên thâm</p>
<p>John is more serious and scholarly than his brother.</p>
<p>Her research was published in a scholarly journal.</p>
<p>26. scholarship (n) /ˈskɑːlərʃɪp/: học bổng</p>
<p>He got /won a scholarship to Harvard.</p>
<p>Paula went to the Royal College of Music on a scholarship.</p>
<p>27. achievement /əˈtʃiːvmənt / (n): thành tích</p>
<p>An Olympic silver medal is a remarkable achievement for one so young.</p>
<p>The Tale of Genji has been described as the greatest achievement of Japanese literature.</p>
<p>It gives you a sense of achievement if you actually make it to the end of a very long book.</p>
<p>28. achieve (v) /əˈtʃiːv/: đạt được</p>
<p>The government's training policy, he claimed, was achieving its objectives.</p>
<p>She finally achieved her ambition to visit South America.</p>
<p>I've been working all day, but I feel as if I've achieved nothing.</p>
<p>29. achiever (n) /əˈtʃiːvər/: người đạt được thành tựu</p>
<p>All the women interviewed were achievers in their chosen field.</p>
<p>High achievers traditionally come from middle-class areas and go to university rather than colleges.</p>
<p>30. achievable (adj) /əˈtʃiːvəbl/: có thể đạt được</p>
<p>Before you set your targets, make sure that they are achievable.</p>
<p>31. engrave /ɪnˈɡreɪv/ (v): khắc, trạm trổ</p>
<p>The jeweller skilfully engraved the initials on the ring.</p>
<p>The bracelet was engraved with his name and date of birth.</p>
<p>32. engraver /ɪnˈɡreɪvər/ (n): thợ khắc</p>
<p>Only three engravers in the pottery industry are involved in the whole of the year.</p>
<p>33. engraving (n) /ɪnˈɡreɪvɪŋ/: tranh điêu khắc</p>
<p>The museum owns many fine 18th-century engravings.</p>
<p>The book describes the art of engraving.</p>
<p>34. feudalism /ˈfjuːdəlɪzəm/ (n): chế độ phong kiến</p>
<p>He furthered some of the ideals of the French Revolution by abolishing feudalism.</p>
<p>the shift from feudalism to capitalism in Europe during the 18th and 19th centuries</p>
<p>35. feudalistic /ˌfjuːdəˈlɪstɪk/ (adj): phong kiến</p>
<p> In feudalistic times, poverty was primarily a function of being deprived of land.</p>
<p>36. construction /kənˈstrʌk∫n/ (n): công trình xây dựng</p>
<p>Construction began this year and will take approximately 18 months.</p>
<p>37. construct /kənˈstrʌkt / (v): xây dựng</p>
<p>The walls are constructed of concrete.</p>
<p>38. construct /ˈkɑːnstrʌkt / (n): xây dựng</p>
<p>His reputation as an eccentric is largely a media construct.</p>
<p>39 constructive /kənˈstrʌktɪv/ (adj): mang tính xây dựng</p>
<p>She criticized my writing, but in a way that was very constructive.</p>
<p>If you don't have anything constructive to say, it's better to say nothing.</p>
<p>40. constructively /kənˈstrʌktɪvli/ (adv): cấu tạo, mang tính xây dựng</p>
<p>We ought to deal constructively with the problems.</p>
<p>Not all pupils will work constructively with other children in the class.</p>
<p>41. constructor /kənˈstrʌktər/ (n): người chế tạo</p>
<p>The firm produces kits for amateur car constructors.</p>
<p>42. constructional /kənˈstrʌkʃənl/ (adj): (thuộc) lãnh vực xây dựng, (thuộc) cấu trúc, (thuộc) cơ cấu</p>
<p>Though they couldn't be listed individually, they could result from a constructional idiom containing variables that permit recursion.</p>
<p>43. maintenance /ˈmeintinəns/ (n): sự bảo dưỡng, tu sửa</p>
<p>The school pays for heating and the maintenance of the buildings.</p>
<p>44. maintain /meɪnˈteɪn/ (v): duy trì, bảo tồn </p>
<p>The two countries have always maintained close relations.</p>
<p>45. admission fee /ədˈmɪʃn fiː/ (n): phí nhập học</p>
<p>The admission fee to the zoo is cheap.</p>
<p>46. admissible /ədˈmɪsəbl/ (adj): chấp nhận được</p>
<p>Photographs are usually admissible evidence provided it can be proved that they are authentic.</p>
<p>The claim was not admissible under the current policy.</p>
<p>47. admissibility /ədˌmɪsəˈbɪləti/ (n): sự chấp nhận</p>
<p>He planned to challenge the admissibility of Paul's confession.</p>
<p>Defence attorneys challenged the admissibility of fingerprint evidence.</p>
<p>48. merchant /ˈmə:t∫ənt / (n): nhà buôn</p>
<p>Experienced merchants said that the fee structure for accepting cards is confusing.</p>
<p>Local merchants experienced a revenue boost in the lead up to Thanksgiving.</p>
<p>49. merchantable /ˈmɜːrtʃəntəbl/ (adj): có thể buôn bán </p>
<p>The poor packing affected the merchantable quality of the goods.</p>
<p>50. ornament /ˈɔ:nəment / (n): đồ trang trí</p>
<p>There were a few china ornaments on the shelf above the fireplace.</p>
<p>51. ornamental /ˌɔːrnəˈmentl/ (adj): có tính chất trang hoàng, có tính chất trang trí, có tính chất trang sức; để trang trí, để trang sức</p>
<p>The chimney pots are purely ornamental.</p>
<p>52. ornamentation /ˌɔːrnəmenˈteɪʃn/ (n): sự trang hoàng, sự trang trí</p>
<p>The architect was instructed to keep ornamentation to a minimum.</p>
<p>53. ornament /ˈɔːrnəment / (v): trang trí</p>
<p>The building relies on clever design rather than on ornament for its impressive effect.</p>
<p>54. certify /ˈsə:tifai/ (v): chứng nhận</p>
<p>As a young man, he had been certified and sent to a hospital for the mentally ill.</p>
<p>55. certifiable /ˈsɜːrtɪfaɪəbl/ (adj): có thể chứng nhận</p>
<p>Simon's washing his car again - that man's certifiable!</p>
<p>56. certifiably /ˈsɜːrtɪfaɪəbli/ (adv): có thể xác nhận</p>
<p>He's a convicted felon, a certifiably loathsome human being.</p>
<p>57. certificate /sərˈtɪfɪkət / (n/v): chứng chỉ, bằng cấp</p>
<p>She has a Certificate in Drama Education.</p>
<p>58. certification /ˌsɜːrtɪfɪˈkeɪʃn/ (n): giấy chứng nhận</p>
<p>He earned certification to fly single-engine aircraft.</p>
<p>Fairtrade is a certification that guarantees producers in the developing world are paid a fair price for their crops.</p>
<p>59. ancient /ˈein∫ənt / (adj): cổ kính</p>
<p>Archaeologists are excavating the ruined temples of this ancient civilization.</p>
<p>60. anciently /ˈeɪnʃəntli/ (adv): xưa</p>
<p>The area where the market was anciently held .</p>
<p>61. formerly /ˈfɔ:məli/ (adv): trước kia, trước đây</p>
<p>The position of our formerly illegal workers has now been regularized.</p>
<p>The artist formerly known as Prince.</p>
<p>62. former /ˈfɔːrmər/ (adj): trước đây, lúc trước</p>
<p>This fine ruin was, in former times, a royal castle.</p>
<p>This beautiful old building has been restored to its former glory.</p>
<p>63. recommend /rekəˈmend / (v): gợi ý, đề nghị</p>
<p>I can recommend the chicken in mushroom sauce - it's delicious.</p>
<p>She has been recommended for promotion.</p>
<p>64. recommendation /ˌrekəmenˈdeɪʃn/ (n):sự giới thiệu</p>
<p>We accept the key recommendations of the report.</p>
<p>65. precious (adj) /ˈˈpreʃəs/: quý giá</p>
<p>Clean water is a precious commodity in many parts of the world.</p>
<p>66. preciousness /ˈpreʃəsnəs/ (n): sự quý giá</p>
<p>I have always had a sense of the preciousness of life.</p>
<p>As an elder person, part of my role is to try to keep alive the preciousness of history.</p>"
